  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_29c3a9a3-1e20-4e71-92f8-478e37bb1dbe'
      });

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer12605529710898666943">In a land where three suns almost never set, a fledgling killer joins a school of assassins, seeking vengeance against the powers who destroyed her family.<br/><br/>Daughter of an executed traitor, Mia Corvere is barely able to escape her father’s failed rebellion with her life. Alone and friendless, she hides in a city built from the bones of a dead god, hunted by the Senate and he</span>
  <span id="freeText12605529710898666943" style="display:none">In a land where three suns almost never set, a fledgling killer joins a school of assassins, seeking vengeance against the powers who destroyed her family.<br /><br />Daughter of an executed traitor, Mia Corvere is barely able to escape her father’s failed rebellion with her life. Alone and friendless, she hides in a city built from the bones of a dead god, hunted by the Senate and her father’s former comrades. But her gift for speaking with the shadows leads her to the door of a retired killer, and a future she never imagined.<br /><br />Now, Mia is apprenticed to the deadliest flock of assassins in the entire Republic—the Red Church. If she bests her fellow students in contests of steel, poison and the subtle arts, she’ll be inducted among the Blades of the Lady of Blessed Murder, and one step closer to the vengeance she desires. But a killer is loose within the Church’s halls, the bloody secrets of Mia’s past return to haunt her, and a plot to bring down the entire congregation is unfolding in the shadows she so loves.<br /><br />Will she even survive to initiation, let alone have her revenge?</span>
  <a data-text-id="12605529710898666943" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">The setting is a collision between ancient Rome and merchant prince Venice. The world really started as a thought experiment - what would've happened <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">The setting is a collision between ancient Rome and merchant prince Venice. The world really started as a thought experiment - what would've happened if Julius Caesar's bid to overthrow the Roman republic failed and the Republic itself survived to the middle ages?<br /><br />With, you know, blood magic and living shadows and whatnot thrown in for good measure :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1697907012" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1697907012" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1697907012?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2016">2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1697907012" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13005976033686952731"><blockquote>
  <i>"The three suns hanging on a chain about his throat tried to gleam, but the clouds in the crying sky told them no."</i>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468854321ra/19752669.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>If I were to write a review in the style of this book, it would begin something like this:<br/><br/><i>I turned these pieces of former tree, the midnight ink recounting a narrative tumefied by metaphoric wanderings. It pained, O readers, it pained! Persevere, I thought. Quitting now would be a mark of failure, like a baby bird that flutters its wings for the very first time, stretching them </i></span>
  <span id="freeText13005976033686952731" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"The three suns hanging on a chain about his throat tried to gleam, but the clouds in the crying sky told them no."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468854321ra/19752669.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I were to write a review in the style of this book, it would begin something like this:<br><br><i>I turned these pieces of former tree, the midnight ink recounting a narrative tumefied by metaphoric wanderings. It pained, O readers, it pained! Persevere, I thought. Quitting now would be a mark of failure, like a baby bird that flutters its wings for the very first time, stretching them out with the promise, the hope, of flight, only to return, defeated, to its nest.</i><br><br><u>I didn't finish it</u>. Judge away, O readers, judge away, but I could not force myself through. <b>It was a nightmare</b>. I was so freaking bored. And I had to go read the blurb to remind myself what the book was about. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> is so difficult to get through that I got to a point where I was just counting the pages until I could return to Tana French. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/338798.Ulysses" title="Ulysses by James Joyce" rel="nofollow noopener">Ulysses</a> is easier to read than this book.<br><br>You know what it reminds me of? <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a>
</b>. A denser version. I once said that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10429045.Shatter_Me__Shatter_Me___1_" title="Shatter Me (Shatter Me, #1) by Tahereh Mafi" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me</a> was not a novel; it was a collection of similes and metaphors that do not make sense. That is a fantastic description for this book! <b>A collection of similes and metaphors that do not make sense</b>. Clearly this works for a lot of people, but it was not for me.<br><br>The book is <b>heavy</b>. Lots of descriptions, overuse of similes and metaphors (did I mention that they don't make sense?) until I had no idea what was going on. I read sentences and thought "Huh?!" It hurt trying to figure out what Kristoff was saying. <br><br>There were the ones that I understood but were so eyeroll-worthy that I wished I didn't:<br><blockquote>
  <i>"Mia sighed. Took her temper by the earlobe and pulled it to heel."</i>
</blockquote><br>And then there were all the ones that I really just didn't understand:<br><blockquote>
  <i>The girl felt the words in her chest. In the deepest, darkest place, where the hope children breathe and adults mourn withered and fell away, floating like ashes on the wind.<br>**<br>If her face were a puzzle, most would put it back in the box, unfinished.<br>**<br>Something had followed her from that place. The place above the music where her father died. Something hungry. A blind, grub consciousness, dreaming of shoulders crowned with translucent wings. And she, who would gift them.</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1468855369ra/19752900.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>No, seriously, what the fuck is happening?</b><br><br>And everything is so <b>overwritten and melodramatic</b>. To borrow the quote <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575835186?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Anna</a> used: <i>"She introduced her boot to his partner's groin, kicking him hard enough to cripple his unborn children."</i><br><br>???????????????? Just say you kicked him in the balls! ^This does not better writing make.<br><br>I can't do it. I'm going to go bury myself in a place where love blossoms and life finds itself carried away on the wings of wonder. <b>Read a better book, that is.</b><br><br><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://society6.com/bookgeek/" rel="nofollow noopener">Store</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13005976033686952731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1291440237" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1291440237" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1291440237?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=why-do-i-hate-myself">why-do-i-hate-myself</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1291440237" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9330111505249654914">Allow me to pay homage to the writing style of this book.<br/><br/>Finished the book. I sigh. Twisted my head. Arched my back like a mewling kitten towards its mother, hungry, afraid, an innocent newcomer in this cruel, cold world. My head ached. An unbelievable pain like a knife to the head, hilt broken like a katana sword struck by a bullet, in a fight between a samurai and a cowboy. I sat up. The chair let out a squeak, the noise of an newborn mouse. How can I describe the pain. The suffering! The eter</span>
  <span id="freeText9330111505249654914" style="display:none">Allow me to pay homage to the writing style of this book.<br /><br />Finished the book. I sigh. Twisted my head. Arched my back like a mewling kitten towards its mother, hungry, afraid, an innocent newcomer in this cruel, cold world. My head ached. An unbelievable pain like a knife to the head, hilt broken like a katana sword struck by a bullet, in a fight between a samurai and a cowboy. I sat up. The chair let out a squeak, the noise of an newborn mouse. How can I describe the pain. The suffering! The eternal twilight of the endless night. The soul-sucking misery. The mind-numbing boredom worse than any kind of liquid nitrogen reaching 0 Kelvin. O hapless imagery! O destruction of the English language. How I beseech thee, book, to stop thus!<br /><br />Ok, I'm done. I hurt myself writing that.<br /><br />Do you like descriptions? No, I mean, do you <i>really</i> like descriptions? Do you like <b>overwrought metaphors</b> and a <b>criminal use of adjectives</b>? If you do, then dang diddly if this book isn't written just for you!<br /><br />I read my fair share of bodice rippers. Books in which a love scene is dragged out in excrutiating minutiae and flowery language so flowery you could choke on the scent (see what I did there? Har har har). I have rarely read a love scene so overblown and contrived as the --honestly, I don't know what to call it -- <i>thing</i> at the beginning of this book. <br /><br />And that's just the beginning. To sum it up: the writing is atrocious (to me, who knows, you might like it), <b>the plot is convoluted and barely detectable between the clusterfuckery of purple prose.</b><br /><br />Reader, I abandoned this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9330111505249654914" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2151534270" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2522587174303852657">Let me start by saying… <b>HOLY SHIT.</b><br/><br/>Look, I doubted you my people. I sometimes don’t believe everyone when they rave about a book because too often I find they’re overhyped. <br/><br/>Well you were right, I should have believed you. So now that this is out of the way…<br/><br/><b>This. Was. Epic.</b><br/><br/>Loved the world, loved the magic system, loved the characters, loved the story, loved the humor... I JUST LOVED IT ALL.<br/><br/>The first chapter is straight up painful. The writing style won't be for everyone (I had no issues with it!).</span>
  <span id="freeText2522587174303852657" style="display:none">Let me start by saying… <b>HOLY SHIT.</b><br /><br />Look, I doubted you my people. I sometimes don’t believe everyone when they rave about a book because too often I find they’re overhyped. <br /><br />Well you were right, I should have believed you. So now that this is out of the way…<br /><br /><b>This. Was. Epic.</b><br /><br />Loved the world, loved the magic system, loved the characters, loved the story, loved the humor... I JUST LOVED IT ALL.<br /><br />The first chapter is straight up painful. The writing style won't be for everyone (I had no issues with it!). The footnotes need some getting used to but it just made me dive deeper into the world and wouldn't want them to not be there now.<br /><br />There are two cringy sex scenes but I hate them in general so it's fine. The romance didn't take over the whole story. <br /><br />I will be reading book 2 asap and will be slowly dying as I wait for book 3!<br /><br />I don't just recommend it, I'm actually asking you to read it. <br /><br />I don't give 5 stars often so that says it all!</span>

<div id="review_1406963995" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1406963995" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1406963995?book_show_action=true">Oct 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=never-again">never-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1406963995" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6217451283369227921"><strong>I can’t… finish this.</strong><br/><br/>Just thinking about it makes my head ache.<br/><br/>The writing is so… <em>thick.</em> Like every message, action, description that is meant to reach the reader through it is compressed to the point where trying to dismantle it takes too much energy.<br/><br/>If that’s not a reason to prematurely close a book, I don’t know what is.<br/><br/>The truth is, I think I would have liked this, had it not been written in such a painful way and had it not possessed flashbacks meant, it seemed, more to confuse us than anyt</span>
  <span id="freeText6217451283369227921" style="display:none"><strong>I can’t… finish this.</strong><br /><br />Just thinking about it makes my head ache.<br /><br />The writing is so… <em>thick.</em> Like every message, action, description that is meant to reach the reader through it is compressed to the point where trying to dismantle it takes too much energy.<br /><br />If that’s not a reason to prematurely close a book, I don’t know what is.<br /><br />The truth is, I think I would have liked this, had it not been written in such a painful way and had it not possessed flashbacks meant, it seemed, more to confuse us than anything else.<br /><br />I really didn’t have a formidable reading experience with <em>Nevernight.</em> This was my first Jay Kristoff book, one I was looking extremely forward to, but boy do I want to stay away from this author in the future. My poor head.<br /><br />The story looked <em>badass, </em>actually badass, with assassins and revenge plots and kills and vendetta and darkness and fantasy. I couldn’t wait to dive into it.<br /><br />But the reality is different. First, it’s more perplexing than original and the so-called world-building that we’re introduced to is overshadowed by the horrendous writing style full of figures of style I wanted to smother more than decorticate… and the heroine.<br /><br />The heroine whom, may I add, is a demon. I think? She’s awful. Any semblance of emotion that she may have been able to make her body feel in the past is gone, and now, only darkness slithers under her skin.<br /><br />That should have made me <em>love </em>her. It should have. Alas, I felt no connection to her whatsoever and couldn’t even cheer her on her killings – which I’m usually glad to do, for antiheroes.<br /><br />Sometimes I feel a little sad about not finishing a book, but in this case? God no. Stay away from me, <em>Nevernight.</em> I mean it.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6217451283369227921" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1902793356" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1902793356" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1902793356?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=erotic-scenes">erotic-scenes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1902793356" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17969113862039552138"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The last thing you will ever be in this world, girl, is someone’s hero. But you will be a girl heroes fear.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>I feel like this book is extremely polarizing but if you love it, you will love it completely and whole heartedly. If you love it, you won’t be able to put it down. If you love it, you will probably consider it one of the best book you’ll read all year. And I loved it. I loved it so much. Even though, when I look through my friends’ reviews, I feel like I’m in the minority. Bu</span>
  <span id="freeText17969113862039552138" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The last thing you will ever be in this world, girl, is someone’s hero. But you will be a girl heroes fear.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I feel like this book is extremely polarizing but if you love it, you will love it completely and whole heartedly. If you love it, you won’t be able to put it down. If you love it, you will probably consider it one of the best book you’ll read all year. And I loved it. I loved it so much. Even though, when I look through my friends’ reviews, I feel like I’m in the minority. But for me, <i>Nevernight</i> is worth all of the hype. <br><br>I will say that I personally feel like this is an adult fantasy novel, not a YA fantasy novel, despite the characters age. There is sex, a lot of sex, and violence, a whole lot of violence, and gore, don’t forget all of the gore! So please go into this book knowing this, and knowing that this is a very mature book in general.<br><br>Also, before I get into my review, I want to address the problematic, hurtful, and harmful representation of the Māori people (the indigenous Polynesian people of New Zealand) that Jay Kristoff was inspired to base the Dweymeri race in this book from. Jay has stated, <a href="https://twitter.com/misterkristoff/status/806129828109746176" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>“the tatts aren’t based off Māori designs”</i>
</a> but it still feels a little bad while you’re reading this story, even if the Dweymeri are not direct representatives of the Māori. I just think it’s important to bring this discussion up and I want everyone to know about this controversy surrounding the portrayal of this culture. I, also, do not want anyone to think that I’m making excuses for it, because I am definitely not even though I did love this book. Cultural appropriation and reinforcing stereotypes will never be okay and I truly wish this element was not a part of this book, but it is, and I’m not going to not bring it to your attention whether you believe it is or not. <br><br><i>Nevernight</i> is a story about a sixteen-year-old girl named Mia Corvere, who is on a mission for vengeance and to right the wrong that has been done to her family in the only way she knows how: killing everyone. Mia find her way into the Red Church, who worship the Goddess of murder, where she is training to become one of the deadliest assassins of all time. Also, Mia has an affinity for the shadows, which not only grants her the only companion she has ever known, but also sends her on a quest to discover more about her powers and who she really is. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The brighter the light, the deeper the shadows”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This story reads like a dark version of <i>Harry Potter</i>, to me. From the boarding school aspect, to the magic, to how they travel through the world, to the professors and their different classes, so much of this book reminds me of the wizarding world.<br><br>And even though this is a series, there is no real cliffhanger (even though you will be left wanting more), this is a full standing book that has an amazing story and that you could just read on its own. I’m not sure the last time I read a book in a fantasy series that did that. <br><br>This book is so sex positive, and the opening chapter of this book was so beautifully done. It is one of my favorite first chapters of all time, and I think Jay Kristoff is nothing short of a genius to have been able to write a juxtaposition that well. I mean, Jay’s writing is lyrical and beautiful, too, but it’s so damn smart that I can’t help but be in awe of this story he has crafted. <br><br> And Mia’s bisexuality is so beautifully on display. Like, all I want in my reading life is girl assassins loving each other and saving the world, and this book doesn’t disappoint, even though the main "love" story is hetero. We need more stories with queer main protagonists that are normalized and just having their adventures and story told without a coming out story or an explanation on why they feel the way they do. Again, Jay Kristoff gets all the kudos and credit. <br><br>I always pride myself in being able to see the twists coming, and I was completely blindsided by the end reveal of <i>Nevernight</i>! Also, for those of you who have finished, I will go down with that hate to love ship. I. WILL. GO. DOWN. WITH. THAT. SHIP. <br><br>And finally, if you find yourself loving this series and wanting more, I can’t recommend Mark Lawrence’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1896170593" rel="nofollow noopener">Red Sister</a> enough! It’s a very reminiscent story, with perhaps more violence, but with definitely less sex, and both star queer assassin nun-like characters who study at a church. <br><br><i>Nevernight</i> was everything that I never knew I wanted, and it is totally just as amazing as some of the most popular and highly acclaimed adult fantasy series out there. This novel meant so very much to me, and I cannot wait to start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2159863289" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a> as soon as humanly possible! Happy reading, everyone! <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508814581i/24257005._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The books we love, they love us back. And just as we mark our places in the pages, those pages leave their marks on us. I can see it in you, sure as I see it in me. You’re a daughter of words. A girl with a story to tell.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br>Buddy read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/43359632-katherine-x1f319---paperbackdreamer" rel="nofollow noopener">Katherine</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a>, &amp; <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7345713-paloma" rel="nofollow noopener">Paloma</a>! ❤</span>
  <a data-text-id="17969113862039552138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2511907507" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2511907507" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2511907507?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-popsugar-reading-challenge">2018-popsugar-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=best-of-decade">best-of-decade</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2511907507" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11831270430244511911">4.5 stars <blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567374890i/28085589._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
  <br/>
  <br/>
  <i>The brighter the light, the deeper the shadow.</i>
</blockquote>Mia Corvere used to be the daughter of a respectable family but <b>all that changes </b>when her father is strung up for leading a rebellion. <blockquote>
  <i>'Never Flinch.' A cold whisper in her ear. 'Never fear. And never, ever forget.'<br/>The girl nodded slowly.<br/>Exhaled the hope inside. </i>
</blockquote>Just ten years old, Mia watches her father dance at the end of a rope and silently<b> swears revenge upon them all. </b><br/><br/>But in order to <b>extract her revenge,</b> she first need</span>
  <span id="freeText11831270430244511911" style="display:none">4.5 stars <blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567374890i/28085589._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>The brighter the light, the deeper the shadow.</i>
</blockquote>Mia Corvere used to be the daughter of a respectable family but <b>all that changes </b>when her father is strung up for leading a rebellion. <blockquote>
  <i>'Never Flinch.' A cold whisper in her ear. 'Never fear. And never, ever forget.'<br>The girl nodded slowly.<br>Exhaled the hope inside. </i>
</blockquote>Just ten years old, Mia watches her father dance at the end of a rope and silently<b> swears revenge upon them all. </b><br><br>But in order to <b>extract her revenge,</b> she first needs training. For the next six years, she learns all she can in order to pledge her allegiance to (and receive training from) <b>the Red Church </b> and the Lady of Blessed Murder.<br><br>The Red Church trains assassins every year but only a few make it to the final stages. Mia will have to come in top of class in either <b>blades, poisons, manipulation or thievery. </b><br><br>Mia does have<b> a "secret" weapon </b>in the form of Mr. Kingly, a vaguely cat-shaped shadow creature who feeds upon her fear and in exchange obeys her in battle.<br><br>With deadly assassins on every side, will Mia triumph? <b>Will she even make it out alive?</b><blockquote>
  <i>You'll be a rumor. A whisper. The thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. The last thing you will ever be, girl, is someone's hero.</i>
</blockquote> <b>Wow. This one was addicting!</b><br><br>There were so many things that <b>absolutely worked</b> in this novel that I had a tough time putting this down. I loved the World Building, the Tone and the Side Characters.<br><br><u>
  <b>The World Building</b>
</u><br><br>Mia lives in a world with three rotating suns (hence Nevernight) and the author did a fabulous of incorporating that in the book. I also really enjoyed all of the little details he includes - like the sand creatures or the odd customs from the other characters. <br><br>The lore from their religion really helped ground such a fantastical world. Also, I enjoyed that the Gods weren't imaginary - that they were real and they did influence the human world.<br><br><u>
  <b>The Tone</b>
</u><br><br>I really expected this to be a MB - but it ended up being like <b> Harry Potter with a deadly twist</b>.<br><br> With Mia and the other assassins going on adventures and misadventures, the whole book ended up being far more lighthearted than I imagined.<blockquote><i>Beauty you're born with, but brains you earn.</i></blockquote>There were areas where I was surprised by the violence but the main character had such a<b> cute-yet-deadly </b>take on things that the book was not overbearingly dark.<br><br><u><b>The Side Characters</b></u><br><br>This is an absolutely amazing. Jay Kristoff pulled out all the stops with the quirky, weird and wonderful secondaries. Honestly, the side characters made this book shine.<br><br>I loved the odd dynamic between the twins (Kristoff really brought this one to life!) - they were so creepy and fascinating. All of the masters at the school were so interesting - I really wish we could've spent more time with them.<br><br>Also, I adored Mr. Kindly - he is the<b> best evil(ish) shadow cat </b>in existence. His <b>ruthlessness </b>towards the world and his love for his human made him absolutely perfect.<br><br>And who could resist that little the bit of romance blooming between Tric and Mia (though, with that ending...ooooo....Kristoff has a lot of explaining to do!).<br><br><b><u>Overall</u></b><br><br>Really, truly enjoyed this one. It did become a bit too much for me at times but overall - yes! Loved it! Cannot wait for the next one!!<br><br><b> Audiobook Comments</b><br>Read by Holter Graham - and wow. He did an amazing job with the audio. The only thing that threw me off was Tric's voice. He sounded more like an old man who smoked one too many cigarettes than a teenage kid in love.<br><br><i>The 2018 POPSUGAR Reading Challenge - a book about death or grief</i><br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_1575835186" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575835186" />
    <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner"><img alt="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532688964p2/31461418.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1575835186?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=in-a-minority-here">in-a-minority-here</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=2016-reads">2016-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=authors-i-will-never-read-again">authors-i-will-never-read-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=arcs-2016">arcs-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575835186" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2659801750717738326"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468786156i/19746105._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <u>UPDATE</u>
</b> : Because it seems that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_' title='Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevernight</a> wasn't shitty enough as it was, it also shows <b>problematic rep for Maori.</b> Please read <a href='http://anjuliewritesstuff.weebly.com/blog/racism-author-accountability-and-nevernight' rel='nofollow noopener'>Anjulie's brilliant post</a> about it.<br/><br/><b>MY EYES, O, MY EYES!</b> O, gentlefriends, you may not approve of my decision to rate <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_' title='Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevernight</a> with a severe and lonely star given the fact that I failed to finish it. But I tried, O, gentlefriends, trust me, I tried, yet completing the task of reading all 18,695 pages of this wonder-<br/><br/><i>There are only 448 pages...</i><br/><br/>Oh, FUCK OFF, the cat "wh</span>
  <span id="freeText2659801750717738326" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1468786156i/19746105._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>UPDATE</u>
</b> : Because it seems that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> wasn't shitty enough as it was, it also shows <b>problematic rep for Maori.</b> Please read <a href="http://anjuliewritesstuff.weebly.com/blog/racism-author-accountability-and-nevernight" rel="nofollow noopener">Anjulie's brilliant post</a> about it.<br><br><b>MY EYES, O, MY EYES!</b> O, gentlefriends, you may not approve of my decision to rate <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> with a severe and lonely star given the fact that I failed to finish it. But I tried, O, gentlefriends, trust me, I tried, yet completing the task of reading all 18,695 pages of this wonder-<br><br><i>There are only 448 pages...</i><br><br>Oh, FUCK OFF, the cat "who is not a cat" (why thank you I KNOW you told me one billion times already - go haunt someone else's shadow, watch over another balcony with your not-eyes would you even though I don't even want to know how THAT bloody works)<br><br>Truth is, O, gentlefriends, I'm taking my life back. <b>The 42% I read were painfully indigestible and I am very sorry if I offend 99% of my friends who love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4735144.Jay_Kristoff" title="Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Jay Kristoff</a>'s writing but I cannot do this. I CANNOT</b>. <br><br><b>1) <u>The metaphors and similes</u></b><br><br>First, I don't like them as a whole. While I do believe that they can add a poetic touch to a novel, if I start highlighting them, it either means that : <br><br>a) they're <b>overused</b> ; <br>b) they <b>don't make any kind of sense</b> ; <br>c) they make me forget the story to focus on the prose, as if the writer was tapping me on the shoulder in a "I am so clever, am I not?" fashion.<br><br><u>Some of them made me roll my eyes</u>.<br><br><i>"Mia caught her temper by the collar, gave it a good hard shake. Clearing her throat, she brushed her crooked fringe from her eyes."</i><br><br><i>"Mia sighed. Took her temper by the earlobe and pulled it to heel."</i><br><br><u>Others earned a well-deserved WTF?!</u> <br><br><i>"Tric gave another half-hearted stab, but the beast had forgotten its quarry entirely, great eyes rolling as it flipped over and over, dragging its bulk back below the sand, <b>howling like a dog who's just returned home from a hard turn's work to find another hound in his kennel, smoking his cigarillos and in bed with his wife</b>."</i><br><br>O_o<br><br><i>"They're led by a dozen camels, Tric. A noseless dog could follow this trail of shit in the middle of truedark. If they suddenly start trekking <b>faster than a forty-a-turn smoker with an armload of drunken prostitutes</b>, I think we can find them again."</i><br><br>????!?!!<br><br><b>2) <u>Heavy wordiness and other useless descriptions</u></b><br><br>This is a matter of taste, alright? But I can't do this? Not willingly, at least? Look, I graduated in French Literature and hence have had my fair share of wordy books for the sake of being wordy. After five years, I've come to the conclusion that <b>this overwritten and purple writing style does not suit me</b>. Words are meant to <b>carry the story</b>, and not to prove how clever and well-read the author is. Again, in my opinion anyway.<br><br><i>"She introduced her boot to his partner's groin, kicking him hard enough to cripple his unborn children."</i><br><br>BECAUSE THAT'S A THING. <br><br>Nope. That's <b>a commonplace</b>. <br><br>I tend to find commonplaces useless. <br><br><i>"The horizon was crusted like a beggar's lips, scoured by winds laden with voices just beyond hearing. The second sun kissing the horizon was usually the sign for Itreya's brutal winters to begin, but out there, the heat was still blistering."</i><br><br>Many of you might adore this writing. I do not. Oh, and no, before some gentle soul implies it, it is not because I'm "used to YA" or "unable to 'get it'". As I said, I can enjoy classics. Just not the ones that make me want to pull my hair out. <br><br><b>3) <u>There are footnotes as a world-building</u></b><br><br>Call it as you want, when an author uses LONG footnotes to narrate parts of the world-building, it seems like <b>info-dumping</b> to me. And an annoying one, at that. Honestly? I stopped reading them after two chapters : I had a hard time connecting with the story already, and would have DNFed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> way faster if I had stopped every few pages to read these damn footnotes. More generally, <b>I find it lazy to use footnotes when these legends could have been incorporated into the main story</b>. <br><br>There's also a character who speaks like a Shakespeare's lad, but at this point, I'm not even counting anymore. <br><br>As much as I wanted to love <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a>, whose blurb made it sound so captivating, <b>I cannot stand this writing and it spoiled my read</b>. If you add it to the facts that :<br><br>1) The <b>world-building</b> is a mash-up between the Roman Empire, the Venice Republic, Harry Potter and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20821111.The_Young_Elites__The_Young_Elites___1_" title="The Young Elites (The Young Elites, #1) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">The Young Elites</a> (and surely many more) ; <br><br>2) The heroine already earned <b>her special nemesis</b> whose only purpose seems to glare and glare and glare again ; <br><br>3) <b>I don't care</b> about any of the characters whatsoever (except Tric. I did like Tric) ; <br><br>4) I don't appreciate the so-called wit of that fucking cat who is not a cat (I didn't laugh ONCE, alright?) ;<br><br>5) I am BORED ; <br><br>... Well, you'll understand why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26114463.Nevernight__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___1_" title="Nevernight (The Nevernight Chronicle, #1) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> and me will part ways now, at 42%. <br><br>Mark my words, though : this will be a hit. Oh, well. On my minority shelf it goes. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2096875499?book_show_action=true">Aug 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=non-ya">non-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=1-star">1-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2096875499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5303235511033439311">your friendly reminder that i did not care for this book, and <b>my full review is up now on my blog</b>: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2019/11/20/more-unpopular-opinions-because-im-dead-inside/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>now i'm going to hide.<br/><br/>---------------<br/><br/>I simply cannot believe how much I hated this book.<br/><br/>It was on my currently reading shelf for five months. At one point, I noticed I left it in a friend's apartment and I didn’t even mention it for days. Eventually, after weeks passed without me opening the book and I remained unable to even gaze upon it without shuddering, </span>
  <span id="freeText5303235511033439311" style="display:none">your friendly reminder that i did not care for this book, and <b>my full review is up now on my blog</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2019/11/20/more-unpopular-opinions-because-im-dead-inside/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />now i'm going to hide.<br /><br />---------------<br /><br />I simply cannot believe how much I hated this book.<br /><br />It was on my currently reading shelf for five months. At one point, I noticed I left it in a friend's apartment and I didn’t even mention it for days. Eventually, after weeks passed without me opening the book and I remained unable to even gaze upon it without shuddering, I had to hunker down and act like it was a homework assignment.<br /><br />The upside of that was that my actual reading assignments (on the subject of the socioeconomic impact of globalization on Sri Lanka) seemed very interesting in comparison.<br /><br />I think there are some books that have no excuse to be boring. There should be some synopses and plotlines that are just way too creative and objectively fun-sounding to be lame in execution.<br /><br />This is one of them. And yet.<br /><br />This is about assassin boarding school. It’s been described as Hogwarts, but with murder. It’s supposed to be filled with fascinating anti-heroes and humorous asides and a storyline to blow you away.<br /><br />This is what I expected.<br /><br />What I got was a very long book with an inexplicably small (borderline unreadable) font size and tons of footnotes about various mundane details in made-up high-fantasy history delivered in what seemed to be intended to be dry, uproarious humor and instead felt condescending and pretentious and so, so monotonous, not to mention like a crime against sentences. The sex scenes made me cringe (and I’ve read Jay Kristoff described as a male author capable of writing full, realistic female characters, but after the way Mia was sexualized I must beg to differ).<br /><br />Like, of course this is what would happen when A Man writes a book with a female protagonist. Of course she would have absolutely no healthy friendships with women. Of course there’d be more instances of the word “bitch” than of proper verb use. (Yes, I’m still stuck on the sentence structure.) Of course we’d hear nonstop about the “rare treat” of her “curves” and her “bow-shaped lips.” AND OF COURSE THERE’D BE THIS MUCH DISGUSTING TERRIBLE SMUT.<br /><br />Also, for someone whose whole character centers around her not wanting to murder innocents, she’s sure okay with murdering innocents.<br /><br />All I wanted was some action, maybe some nefarious plots and some murder and some backstabbing of both the literal and figurative variety. Which I realize is a lot to ask for...FROM ASSASSIN BOARDING SCHOOL.<br /><br />(It actually doesn’t seem like a lot to ask for from assassin boarding school.)<br /><br />But this book was so, so long, and so, so little of it contained any of that, and what did was so, so drowned in self-serious prose and heavy-handed style and unrelenting monotony (plus smut with enough overwrought description to make bodice-ripper writers shake their heads) as to make it not even fun.<br /><br />This is maybe the most pretentious book I've ever read, and also boring, and also AGAIN WHAT WAS THAT SENTENCE STRUCTURE.<br /><br />I am so glad I’m not reading this anymore.<br /><br />Bottom line: No thank you please forever!<br /><br />---------------<br /><br />reading this book felt like doing homework.<br /><br />except homework would never be so disrespectful to verb use.<br /><br />review to come<br /><br />---------------<br /><br />always a good sign when you totally forget you're reading a book<br /><br />---------------<br /><br />my hobbies include: giving into YA hype but like 2 years after everyone else read it<br /><br />---------------<br /><br />my favorite reviewers have spoken. (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/49148508-maybelline" rel="nofollow noopener">@may</a> <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42163117-emma" rel="nofollow noopener">@emma</a>)<br /><br />it is time to add this to my tbr. <s>where it will probably remain for months</s></span>
  <a data-text-id="5303235511033439311" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1291046248" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1291046248" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1291046248?book_show_action=true">Aug 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/27841061-nevernight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=revolting">revolting</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=best-series-ya">best-series-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=cover-whore">cover-whore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=kickass-heroines">kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=that-bitch-is-cray">that-bitch-is-cray</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=the-book-boy-is-mine">the-book-boy-is-mine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1291046248" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12556957339449006699"><b>2/2/20: taking bets now as to whether or not this reread ends with me reading DARK DAWN.</b> #idontreadlastbooks #issues<br/><br/><b>There seems to be some confusion on the YA/not YA nature of this book, so let the record show, in response to the question, "Are your books YA or not?" on his website FAQ, Kristoff replied:</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>THE NEVERNIGHT CHRONICLE is a different beast. The protagonist is a sixteen year old girl. Does that automatically make it YA? My editors say “Definitely not, and who the hell let you out of y</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12556957339449006699" style="display:none"><b>2/2/20: taking bets now as to whether or not this reread ends with me reading DARK DAWN.</b> #idontreadlastbooks #issues<br><br><b>There seems to be some confusion on the YA/not YA nature of this book, so let the record show, in response to the question, "Are your books YA or not?" on his website FAQ, Kristoff replied:</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>THE NEVERNIGHT CHRONICLE is a different beast. The protagonist is a sixteen year old girl. Does that automatically make it YA? My editors say “Definitely not, and who the hell let you out of your cage? Get back to work”.<br><br>These books are about an assassin. They are, as you may expect, somewhat violent as a result. They also have sex scenes (and now I have to contemplate the fact that my mother is going to read them *shudders*). I’d rate them MA (or NA if you prefer) and describe them as “crossover books”. But they’ll be found in the adult Fantasy section of your bookstore.</i>
</blockquote><br>SO. I stand corrected. <i>Not</i> YA.<br><br><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/08/review-nevernight-by-jay-kristoff-jessicadhaluska-misterkristoff.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>Sometimes you stumble across a book, and, for whatever reason, your expectations are low. Could be the harlequin mask on the cover, could be a previous series by the same author that you were wholly uninterested in, could be a billion different things that are individually insignificant, but cumulatively . . . You turn up you nose. <br><br>O, gentlefriends . . . Do not do unto yourselves the same disservice I almost did unto mine . . . self . . . o.O<br><br>NEVERNIGHT by Jay Kristoff is . . . exquisite.<br><br>I almost didn't read it. Indeed, the release date sneaked up on me, tapped me on the shoulder, and waved hello on Monday afternoon, and I joked to a friend that I should at least update my status on Goodreads and <i>pretend</i> to be reading it . . . Six hours later, it was ten pm, and I was 40% in.<br><br>The first chapter was baffling. Told from two seemingly different perspectives, it chronicles two <i>very different</i> firsts, but uses almost the exact same words. I was internally shouting, "WTF is this?!" but I was curious enough see where it led, and the further I got, the closer the two scenarios spun toward completion, and then it was over, and I saw what he'd done . . . <br><br>In <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/143466.Jabberwocky_and_Other_Poems" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Jabberwocky</a>
</b>, Lewis Carroll turned the English language on its head. He used nonsense words that were decipherable because of his expert manipulation of sentence structure and other, real words that made the meanings of his imaginary words obvious. <br><br>For the first time since I really understood and appreciated what Carroll had wrought, I felt the same kind of glee as I read about a girl losing her virginity and a girl taking her first life. One experience held the potential for the creation of a new life, the other bringing an irrevocable end to a life, and yet . . . He used . . . The same words. <br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1470921090i/19981026.jpg" width="236" height="295" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Riddikulus writing skills aside, the story was also fantastic.<br><br>What's my #1 complaint about assassins in YA fiction?<br><br><b>You:</b> You may have mentioned something about reluctant assassins a time or three.<br><br><b>Me:</b> Damn right.<br><br><b>You:</b> Not a problem here?<br><br><b>Me:</b> *laughs maniacally*<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>People often shit themselves when they die. <br>Their muscles slack and their souls flutter free and everything else just…slips out. For all their audience’s love of death, the playwrights seldom mention it. When the hero breathes his last in the heroine’s arms, they call no attention to the stain leaking across his tights, or how the stink makes her eyes water as she leans in for her farewell kiss. <br>I mention this by way of warning, O, my gentlefriends, that your narrator shares no such restraint.</i>
</blockquote><br>Duly noted, Mr. Narrator, sir.<br><br>And lest you be scared off by visions of graphic and violent death . . . I won't lie, that is part of this story. But only part:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>She’s dead herself, now—words both the wicked and the just would give an eyeteeth smile to hear. A republic in ashes behind her. A city of bridges and bones laid at the bottom of the sea by her hand. And yet I’m sure she’d still find a way to kill me if she knew I put these words to paper. Open me up and leave me for the hungry Dark. But I think someone should at least try to separate her from the lies told about her. Through her. By her. <br>Someone who knew her true. <br>A girl some called Pale Daughter. Or Kingmaker. Or Crow. But most often, nothing at all. A killer of killers, whose tally of endings only the goddess and I truly know. And was she famous or infamous for it at the end? All this death? I confess I could never see the difference. But then, I’ve never seen things the way you have. <br>Never truly lived in the world you call your own. <br>Nor did she, really. <br>I think that’s why I loved her.</i>
</blockquote><br>*goosebumps*<br><br>Mia Covere's tale reminded me a bit of Arya Stark's: a girl whose family is destroyed by politics and hands grasping at power, stumbles into a follower of a most murderous god(dess), and becomes his apprentice. But Mia is more than just a girl . . . She's a girl with a shadow dark enough for two.<br><br><b>You:</b> WTF does that mean?<br><br><b>Me:</b> READ THE BOOK.<br><br>And how many <b>
  <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt2015381" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Guardians of the Galaxy</a>
</b> fans do we have? B/c the coolest part of that movie was the black market space station that was the HEAD OF A CELESTIAL BEING, am I right?<br><br>Well, Mia grew up in Godsgrave, which just might be where the rest of the body fell . . . Okay, it's probably a different being entirely, but the concept is the same, and it's friggin' awesome:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>To the north, the Ribs rose hundreds of feet into the ruddy heavens, tiny windows staring out from apartments carved within the ancient bone. Canals ran out from the hollow Spine . . . </i>
</blockquote><br>My only words of caution are that, if you haven't already cottoned on, there is SEX in this YA novel, which isn't as uncommon as it used to be, but isn't yet unremarkable. And I'm not talking fade-to-black acknowledgment of sexual congress, I'm talking burn-your-ears, think-interesting thoughts-about-the-hands-that-penned-them sex scenes.<br><br>FYI. <br><br>Kristoff calls Mia an assassin who is to death what a maestro is to a symphony, but I felt the same way about Kristoff's manipulation of words and language. Whether Mia slipped into a room <i>like a knife between the ribs</i> or we met a man whose <i>face was more scar than face</i>, this reader felt like she was being spun and tossed by a master. In NEVERNIGHT, Solis might be the Shahiid of Songs, but it was Jay Kristoff who made me dance to the music of his story in ways I've rarely been moved. O so ridiculously highly recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12556957339449006699" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2696620084" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2696620084" />
    <a title="Petrik" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik"><img alt="Petrik" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568016775p2/59458347.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2696620084?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Petrik" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Petrik" href="/user/show/59458347-petrik">Petrik</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008179991" href="/book/show/29845906-nevernight">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Red Sister &amp; Battle-School trope</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Petrik by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/58160628-emily-books-with-emily-fox">Emily (Books with Emily Fox)</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2696620084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1715922601714894928"><b>4.5/5 stars<br/><br/>O’gentlefriend, <i>Nevernight</i> was incredible. Allow me to join The Droogs from now on.</b><br/><br/><i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i> is not a series I’ve never heard of. If you’re active on Book Twitter, Bookstagram, or Booktube, you’ll most likely have seen or heard of this series. How could you not? The fans are very loud and devoted; aesthetically, both US & UK editions of this series look gorgeous as fuck; the content? Let’s just say that the beautiful cover artworks really did the content justice and vic</span>
  <span id="freeText1715922601714894928" style="display:none"><b>4.5/5 stars<br><br>O’gentlefriend, <i>Nevernight</i> was incredible. Allow me to join The Droogs from now on.</b><br><br><i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i> is not a series I’ve never heard of. If you’re active on Book Twitter, Bookstagram, or Booktube, you’ll most likely have seen or heard of this series. How could you not? The fans are very loud and devoted; aesthetically, both US &amp; UK editions of this series look gorgeous as fuck; the content? Let’s just say that the beautiful cover artworks really did the content justice and vice versa. To Emily Fox and Emma, thank you for recommending this book to me. I can’t believe I almost missed such an awesome book just because the series has been falsely labeled as a book/series specifically for YA audience. Now, there’s nothing wrong with YA—this isn’t me judging the quality of YA books—but it feels wrong to immediately label <i>Nevernight</i> or any book as a book targeted for YA audience just because the main character is young; 16 years old in this case. In my opinion, <i>Nevernight</i> sits comfortably in the hybrid stage between YA and adult fantasy; a novel that can be read and enjoyed by both YA &amp; adult SFF reader, just like <i>Mistborn</i> trilogy by Brandon Sanderson or <i>Red Rising Saga</i> (just the first three books) by Pierce Brown. So yes, don’t let the occasional mislabeling of this series put you off from giving the series a go.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Too many books. Too few centuries.”</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br><i>Nevernight</i> is the first book out of three in <i>The Nevernight Chronicle</i> by Jay Kristoff. The story begins with an unnamed narrator telling the readers that they’re going to recount the details behind the tale surrounding the main heroines of the series—Mia Corvere—and from there on we immediately follow Mia’s perspective. There are two timeframes in the narrative, the past where Mia was ten years old; another where Mia is a sixteen years old girl determined to join The Red Church—a school of assassins—to perfect her assassination skills in order to seek vengeance against the people who destroyed her life and family in the past. At its core, <i>Nevernight</i> is a revenge story that utilized a battle-school trope, which is also one of my favorite tropes in SFF. Comparison-wise, I’ll say that if you’ve read and loved <i>Red Sister</i> by Mark Lawrence, you MUST give this book a read. I would describe <i>Nevernight</i> as <i>Red Sister</i> taking place in a setting that’s reminiscent to <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora</i> by Scott Lynch. Revenge, love, and friendship are the three main themes of the novel. Although the plotline may not be the most original one out there, Kristoff’s execution of this dark tale was brilliant.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“The books we love, they love us back. And just as we mark our places in the pages, those pages leave their marks on us. I can see it in you, sure as I see it in me. You're a daughter of the words. A girl with a story to tell.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>How could I not love Mia? She loves solving Puzzle and perusing books, and she also genuinely cares about her loved ones. I’ve mentioned before that <i>Nevernight</i> reminded me of <i>Red Sister</i>. A huge part of this is that I found Mia to be similar to the main heroine of that series: Nona Grey. Both of them are young female main characters learning in a battle-school of assassins; both of them have a similar trait that cares about their friends intensely. I loved seeing Mia’s character development as she learned the true meaning of friendship and love during her deadly lessons in The Red Church. For those of you who don’t know, Mia also has an everlasting companion, Mister Kindly. Mister Kindly is a Daemon in the form of a cat, a devourer of fear that accompanied and helped Mia. Let me repeat that, a shadow cat that devours fear. How can you resist reading this book knowing that Mister Kindly exist!?<br><br><b>Picture: <i>Never Alone</i> by Nan Fe</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1566983326i/28062411._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The world-building in <i>Nevernight</i> isn’t as massive/complex as many adult fantasy series I’ve read. This, however, doesn’t mean that the world-building was poorly done. Three suns that almost never sets, a city built out of the bones of dead giants, families with a long history, and an efficiently told lore that wormed its way into the narrative made The Republic of Itreya filled with a vivid and atmospheric quality. Similar to Camorr from <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora</i>, Itreya reminded me of a fantasy-esque version of Venice. Kristoff incorporated the lore and history of the world effectively into the dark magic and engaging action scenes of the book while leaving questions to be answered in the sequel.<br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“The brighter the light, the deeper the shadow.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Also, I personally think there’s an over-exaggeration over Kristoff’s prose being purplish. Yes, reading is very subjective and his prose won’t be a hit for everyone; no prose ever will. However, the constant screaming I’ve heard about the prose being super purple seemed to imply that reading it will turn the reader into a purple Hulk. I’ll admit that there were a few phrases that I failed to connect with but nothing that major that would end up ruining my enjoyment of the book. Admittedly, one detailed sex scene in this book didn’t work for me, not because it’s not well-written, but it was too long, no pun intended. Thankfully, romance and the sex scenes never took over the story. Generally, I also don’t enjoy reading footnotes, but the footnotes featured in <i>Nevernight</i> provided humorous commentaries and great insights into the world-building that I can’t help but enjoyed reading. Kristoff’s writing and storytelling style were delightful to read; they’re engaging, fun, atmospheric, and beautifully written. <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>“Beauty you're born with, but brains you earn.” </blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br><br>I’ve noticed that there’s a strong feeling that comes with reading <i>Nevernight</i>; it’s either hate it or love it, there’s no in-between. I can finally understand why and fortunately, I’m in the latter. Revenge plot executed wonderfully, filled with empathizing characters and blood-soaked action scenes told in a beautifully dark and enchanting manner; <i>Nevernight</i> is a bloody enthralling start to a trilogy that I enjoyed reading immensely. I’ll be diving into <i>Godsgrave</i> right away. If you haven’t started this series, now is a good time to embark upon this adventure, especially because the third and last book of the trilogy comes out in a few days. The scarlet maestro of assassination has plenty of songs to sing, and you shall never flinch, never forgive, and never forget it.<br><br><b>You can order the book from: <u><a href="http://www.bookdepository.com/book/9781250073020/?a_aid=petrikleo" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository (Free shipping)</a></u></b><br><br><i>You can find <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net/2019/08/28/book-review-nevernight-the-nevernight-chronicle-1-by-jay-kristoff/" rel="nofollow noopener">this</a></u></b> and the rest of my reviews at <b><u><a href="http://novelnotions.net" rel="nofollow noopener">Novel Notions</a></u></b></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1715922601714894928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
