<div id="review_1914778886" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914778886" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1914778886?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008179991" href="/book/show/29845906-nevernight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=lgbtqiap">lgbtqiap</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=the-best-of-the-best">the-best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1914778886" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15933574374924444810"><blockquote>#1 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914778886' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nevernight</a> ★★★★★ <br/>#2 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2283257510' rel='nofollow noopener'>Godsgrave</a> ★★★★★<br/>#3 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2327040689' rel='nofollow noopener'>Darkdawn</a> ??? </blockquote><br/>I already knew that I loved Jay Kristoff’s writing after his contribution to <i>The Illuminae Files</i> series, but I had no idea just how much I would adore his distinct writing voice, the characters and worlds he weaves, or the tremendously emotional stakes and risks that would come into play throughout the course of this brilliant novel. There are books, and then there are <i>stories,</i> with characters who take up so much space in your heart that you </span>
  <span id="freeText15933574374924444810" style="display:none"><blockquote>#1 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1914778886" rel="nofollow noopener">Nevernight</a> ★★★★★ <br />#2 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2283257510" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a> ★★★★★<br />#3 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2327040689" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkdawn</a> ??? </blockquote><br />I already knew that I loved Jay Kristoff’s writing after his contribution to <i>The Illuminae Files</i> series, but I had no idea just how much I would adore his distinct writing voice, the characters and worlds he weaves, or the tremendously emotional stakes and risks that would come into play throughout the course of this brilliant novel. There are books, and then there are <i>stories,</i> with characters who take up so much space in your heart that you could never forget them, and, my friends, Mia Corvere’s tale is a damn <i>story.</i> <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The books we love, they love us back. And just as we mark our places in the pages, those pages leave their marks on us.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><i>Nevernight</i> is widely regarded by many as having a unique (and sometimes difficult to follow) format, due to the footnotes, but I wanted to go ahead and touch upon this before getting into the meat of my review. If you have DNFed this book due to the footnotes, <i>please</i> pick it back up. They are hilarious and odd, and relay a great deal of back story about the world of Godsgrave, but <b>if you have a hard time keeping yourself involved in the story, skip the footnotes and come back to them later.</b> I say this because <i>so many</i> of my friends and followers have told me the footnotes caused them to DNF the book, and that’s a shame, truly, because this is one of the most enjoyable stories I’ve ever read in my life.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“You’ll be a rumor. A whisper. The thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. The last thing you will ever be in this world, girl, is someone’s hero.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Mia Corvere is such a lovable, yet vicious little narrator: despite her bloodthirst and desperate need for vengeance, there’s something a little bit fragile and very young inside of her that I loved so much. It’s like every other scene with her was simultaneously putting me in awe of how clever and strong she could be, yet making me wish I could protect her from the aches of her brutal, bloody past. She’s been through hell and then some, but she has humor for days, and isn’t afraid to let herself care—even if it doesn’t always feel as though it’s in her own best interest.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Walk softly. Learn well. May Our Lady be late when she finds you. And when she does, may she greet you with a kiss.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Much of the true terror of <i>Nevernight</i>, however, comes from the school she attends. Fantasy readers all over the world are familiar with the idea of a protagonist being sent to a boarding school, but Jay’s twist on this is that the “school” Mia seeks out is no Hogwarts—unless Hogwarts replaced Quidditch and Transfiguration with a lot of murder, torture, poisons, and sex. The Red Church is such an incredible setting. It’s painted beautifully vivid, and it’s full of so many mysteries that, no matter how much I learned about it, I constantly felt that I was barely scratching the surface of what it had to offer. I would say, in fact, that just as Mia is one of my new favorite protagonists, the Red Church is easily one of my favorite settings.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>She looked the knife over, this way and that.<br />“Should I give it a name?”<br />“You could, I suppose. But what’s the point?”<br />“It’s this bit.” She touched the blade’s tip. “The part you stick them with.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Of course, it’s not <i>all</i> bloodshed, betrayal, and sex—it’s also a lot of humor, a bit of unlikely alliance-forming (and friendship), and a monster-filled library with the most fascinating and lovable caretaker you’ve ever seen. (Honestly, I could have happily spent chapter upon chapter simply watching Mia sift through this library.) The book also constantly breaks the fourth wall by addressing its reader, which is such a fun and unique spin on storytelling that I found myself constantly tabbing pages for no reason other than the phrasing was so distinct and fantastic. Even if I had never read <i>The Illuminae Files,</i> this book would have quite easily been plenty to convince me that Jay Kristoff belongs on my auto-buy list forever.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“The wolf does not pity the lamb. The storm begs no forgiveness of the drowned.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I could really ramble and gush about this book, and how much I adore Mia, for days on end, but the end result would still be the same: me trying and failing to explain to you all how much I adored this story, how much I desperately want to read everything and anything that Jay <i>ever</i> writes, and how certain I am that each and every one of you needs to pick this book up if you are any sort of fantasy fan at all, because it is truly worth every second of your time.<br /><br />You can find this review and more on my <a href="https://howlinglibraries.com/2018/05/11/nevernight/" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a>, or you can follow me on <a href="https://twitter.com/howlinglibrary" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a>, <a href="https://instagram.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">bookstagram</a>, or <a href="https://facebook.com/howlinglibraries" rel="nofollow noopener">facebook</a>!</span>
  <a data-text-id="15933574374924444810" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2053614881" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2053614881" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2053614881?book_show_action=true">Oct 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008179984" href="/book/show/34503674-nevernight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2053614881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9408350548214213769"><i>”You’ll be a rumour. A whisper. The thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. The last thing you will ever be in this world, girl, is someone’s hero.”</i><br/><br/>Well, I suppose that’s only to be expected when you set out on the dark path of revenge. Not that Mia wouldn’t be able to deal with it. ;-) Truth be told, after reading this book I’m convinced that there is absolutely nothing our heroine wouldn’t be able to deal with. Except of maybe the many bad ratings this book go</span>
  <span id="freeText9408350548214213769" style="display:none"><i>”You’ll be a rumour. A whisper. The thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. The last thing you will ever be in this world, girl, is someone’s hero.”</i><br /><br />Well, I suppose that’s only to be expected when you set out on the dark path of revenge. Not that Mia wouldn’t be able to deal with it. ;-) Truth be told, after reading this book I’m convinced that there is absolutely nothing our heroine wouldn’t be able to deal with. Except of maybe the many bad ratings this book got? *lol* When I started to read <b>“Nevernight”</b> I already knew that I was late to the party, but after reading it and skimming through some of the reviews I also realized that it’s apparently a rather controversial book?! <br /><br />Why the ‘byss I wondered and started to investigate. As it seems most of the reviewers that gave it a low rating just couldn’t with the writing style and the recurring footnotes. Which admittedly, is a valid point. If you’re no fan of paraphrases and poetry or prose I’m fairly certain that you will end up hating this book. So I guess what it truly comes down to is if you’ve liked Tahereh Mafi’s “Shatter Me” series or not. If you loved it there’s a high chance you’ll enjoy the writing style of this book as well, if you hated it, I’d recommend borrowing “Nevernight” from the library and seeing if you enjoy the first few chapters. ;-) <br /><br />As for me, I can only say that I <b>LOVED</b> it! It might have taken me ages to get through this book and the footnotes were kind of distracting at first, but it was definitely worth it! I’ve read so many YA books in my life and even though the initial story of an assassin novice that has to survive her training and initiation is nothing new, the way Jay Kristoff wrote it still managed to give this story a unique spin. This is nothing like Sarah J. Maas’s “Throne of Glass”, this is nothing like Robin Hobb’s “Assassin’s Apprentice”, this was something completely different! Dark, twisted, cunning, cruel, gory, violent and only just a little bit x-rated. ;-P (If you’ve read ACOTAR those scenes won’t shock you though, they are pretty tame in comparison) And of course all the characters are so “morally grey” that they border on obsidian, ebony or jet-black which brings me right to my characters section! XD<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Welcome to the Red Church, where killers are made into proper assassins! You might have the necessary traits but do you also have the guts to improve your skills? Find out and enter the mountain. Where spoilers await you in the darkness, always ready to pounce on you if you happen to cross their path. Or in other, less flowery words: Spoilers ahead! Be careful! *lol*</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Mia Corvere:</b><br /><br /><i>”Never flinch.” A cold whisper in her ear. “Never fear. And never, ever forget.”</i><br /><br />It feels like I’ve been waiting for a heroine like Mia Corvere for my entire life!!! I ADORE this girl! &lt;333 She’s direct, loves books, doesn’t care about anyone’s opinion, curses like a sailor, smokes like a dragon, has a great humour and is kick-ass and cunning af!!! And most of all she feels real!!! Whenever authors try to make their heroines as tough as the male MCs they seem to fail. Jay Kristoff? <b>HE FREAKING NAILED IT!!</b> Well, at least for me he did! It was such a pleasure to follow Mia’s journey. She has the mind of a killer but still shows compassion when no one else does. Throughout the entire book she walks a fine line between becoming a killing machine and trying to keep her humanity. She has no trouble to kill people that hurt the ones she loves, but she draws the line at killing innocents for pleasure and I could have kissed her for refusing to take the final test! &lt;333 Also she was so brave in so many ways! Yes, some might argue that it’s easy to be brave when you have a not-cat that eats your fear, but sometimes bravery means more than just being able to overcome your fears. It’s also brave to stand in front of 5 people that could easily kill you and still refuse to do what they want you to do. So yes, I’m Mia Corvere trash now and I think I might be in love with her. *lol* With both, Mia and Mr. Kindly! Their not-friendship was everything! &lt;333 <br /><br /><i>”Apologies,” Mia frowned, searching the floor as if looking for something. “I appear to have misplaced the fucks I give for what you think...”</i><br /><br /><i>”They can give you a new face, but they can’t give you a new heart. No matter what they take from you, they can’t take that away unless you let them. That’s real strength, Tric. That’s real power.”</i><br /><br /><b>Tric:</b><br /><br /><i>”... You’re a little frightening sometimes, Pale Daughter.”<br />She gave him a wry smile. “Only a little?”<br />“Well, most times, you’re just plain terrifying.”<br />“Come on,” she said, slapping his arm. “I’ll buy you a drink.”</i><br /><br />This Itreyan-Dweymeri boy is so sweet that I instantly loved him! Tric was such a great character and my heart bled for him! The way he got his scars and tattoos? It was so damn painful to read. My poor boy! T_T He was so young and he would have deserved so much better than that! I despise his grandfather Swordbreaker and what he did to him and I adored his mother for loving him so much! Tric’s mom was amazing and I’m sure a lot of his character traits came from her. &lt;3 I could understand his inner conflict about losing his scars though. I mean they basically were his past written on his skin. I agree with Mia though, they don’t define him. Also did anyone find out why he’s named Tric?! I mean he told Mia the story about his scars and tattoos but I can’t remember that he ever told her why he’s named Tric. If any of you know, could you please explain?! (If possible without spoiling too many details if it’s in one of the following two books. *lol*) AND now to the huge WTF moment of this book! I had to read the scene where Ashlinn kills him <b>
  <u>TWICE</u>
</b>, because when I read it for the first time I thought my mind must have played a trick on me! O_o I was so shocked!!! And I’ll never be okay with him dying!! Yes, they are at a school for assassins and there died plenty of the other students throughout the entire book, but TRIC??!! Really? He was one of the two freaking MCs!!! How could Jay do this to us?!! T_T My poor baby boy!!! I’m not okay with this...<br /><br /><i>”Drown him and be done.” His voice dropped to a trembling whisper. “They were her first words. That’s what she fucking named me. Drown him and be done.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Ashlinn:</b><br /><br /><i>”Don’t trouble yourself about what that bitch said,” Ash whispered, glancing at Carlotta’s flawless cheek. “That’s not who you are any more.”<br />“It was never who I was.”<br />Charlotta’s hands fell still. Her stare growing clouded.<br />“It was just who they made me.”</i><br /><br />I really liked Ashlinn and she grew on me until... well, until she freaking killed Tric!!! *lol* How could she? I feel as betrayed by her actions as Mia does! I was on the verge of falling for her character and then she does something like this?! Not nice! &gt;_&lt; And now I find myself second guessing every single thing she said and did in this book. Was it all an act? Did she really like Mia and Carlotta or did she just play games with them? I loved her humour and despite everything she seemed to be a compassionate and nice person. Just like the skilled thief she is, she stole my heart without me even noticing it and now I’m standing in front of the torn ruins of my ribcage. To say it with Mr. Kindly’s words: Dear gentlefriends, I’ve to admit that I’m still wondering about what the hell happened in those last few chapters! Ash’s character arc left me with so many questions I feel a headache coming up! *lol* I can’t wait to see her in “Godsgrave” though, because seriously, there’s no way, I repeat NO FREAKING WAY, she won’t appear in the next book. XD (Or at least I hope so. ;-P)<br /><br /><b>The Shahiids:</b><br /><br /><u>Shahiid Mouser</u> <br /><i>”This is a game, children. But a dangerous one.” He waggled his eyebrows. “The only kind worth playing.”</i><br /><br /><u>Shahiid Aalea</u><br /><i>”Never let your face tell a secret your lips should not.”</i><br /><br /><u>Lord Cassius</u><br /><i>”Killers one, killers all. And each death we bring is a prayer. An offering to Our Lady of Blessed Murder. Death as a mercy. Death as a warning. Death as an end unto itself. All of these, ours to know and gift unto the world. The wolf does not pity the lamb. The storm begs no forgiveness of the drowned.”</i><br /><br />The Shahiids were so amazing! I know I only mentioned a few of them here but when it comes down to it I really liked them all! Shahiid Spiderkiller was so deadly! XD I swear to poison your class frequently just to make sure they actually study is quite the way to motivate your students! *lol* No wonder they all tried to be top at her class. Haha! If your life depends on it poison studies will become your favourite subject. ;-P Shahiid Solis was kind of brutal and cruel so I didn’t like him all too much. I adored Mouser and Aalea though! I’m sure I would have loved to attend their classes. As for Lord Cassius, he seemed to be one of those mysterious characters you never get a grip on and since he died I doubt that I’ll ever understand his reasons and motives. &gt;_&lt; Marielle and Adonai? The Church’s weaver and speaker... well they were just creepy and terrifying! And they obviously had some incestuous relationship going on?! *shudders* I don’t even know how all the girls could swoon over Adonai, for me he was just trouble in a nice disguise. *lol*<br /><br /><b>Chronicler Aelius:</b><br /><br /><i>”The books we love, they love us back. And just as we mark our places in the pages, those pages leave their mark on us. I can see it in you, sure as I see it in me. You’re a daughter of words. A girl with a story to tell.”</i><br /><br />Now here comes one of the characters I loved the most! Chronicler Aelius was legit the best thing about the Red Church!!! That guy was awesome!! I loved the first meeting between him and Mia and that he gave no shit about smoking at the library. *lol* He was like a grumpy puppy that grows on you and moreover he was pretty wise! &lt;3 I adored his stance on books and one of my fave moments was him offering Mia a smoke while they watched the enemy being eaten by the worms. (quite literally) Haha! Also the fact that he is dead!! OMG! That came as a total surprise! He really wasn’t kidding about getting lost in the library and dying there! O_o I really hope there will be more of him in the next book because I need to read more about his intriguing character!!<br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Mia &amp; Tric:</u><br /><br /><i>”As you were kind enough to notice, I’ve fallen a little behind in Songs.”<br />“A little?” Tric snorted. “There’s training dummies up there who could mop the floor with you, Pale Daughter.”<br />“Well, thank you very much,” Mia scowled. “If you’d like to go somewhere and quietly fuck yourself, I’ll be waiting here patiently for your return.”</i><br /><br />Haha! I loved how blunt they were! Those two were always honest with each other and never pretended to be something they are not and I think that might have been the main reason they hit it off. What I really liked about their relationship was that they started as strangers, became sort of best friends and then lovers. It’s rare authors take the time to go for a slow burn and I think this one was done nicely. And yes, in my eyes this was a slow burn because they didn’t do anything until the 60% mark or so? Mia can tell herself about a thousand times that she doesn’t love Tric, we all know better, right? *lol* You don’t go sharing your not-cat with just anyone when you’re about to be whipped by Marielle. &gt;_&lt; To say he was with Mia was such a stupid move but then again he didn’t want her to die and she would have died with a 100 lashes. Still, that they both got 50 in the end was horrible. *swallows* Poor Tric though! I’m sure Mia loved him. That he had to die this way was so cruel. I mean Ash only killed him because he had such an exceptional sense of smell. Such a stupid reason to die! And this might sound weird but it was good for Mia that she killed Swordbreaker and meted out revenge! It won’t bring back Tric but to know that his grandfather eventually got what he deserved must have been liberating for her. At least she could give him that. T_T<br /><br /><i>”For a moment, she wasn’t Mia Corvere, daughter of a murdered house, parched with the thirst for revenge. Not a fledgling assassin or a servant of a goddess. Just a girl. And he a boy. Their eyes blind to all but each other.”</i><br /><br /><u>Mia &amp; Ash:</u><br /><br /><i>”Huzzah! She can be taught!”<br />“Fuck you.”<br />“Fair warning, I’m not much of a biter...”<br />“Ash, I swear to the Mother –“</i> <br /><br />Is it just me or was there a smell of romance in the air? I could have sworn Mia and Ash were attracted by each other. They kind of flirted and they kissed twice! This has to count for something, right? At the moment I don’t see how a relationship between those two could ever work out though. Ash killed Tric who was Mia’s lover and probably her first true love so to say they would be star-crossed lovers would be an understatement par excellence. Still, there was something in the air between those two and I’m sure if Tric would still be alive *sobs* he would actually tell you the same thing! I think before Tric I would have shipped this like crazy, now that I’m so uncertain about Ashlinn’s character I don’t know if I want to ship it or not. I’m kind of torn here. *lol* Maybe Ash will come back in book two and there will be an explanation for how she acted and why she did what she did? Not that an explanation would make me forgive her, but it certainly would help to understand her motives, because right now it’s all Greek to me and I no longer understand the world. XD I’ve yet to decide if I want to board this possible ship or not. ;-P<br /><br /><i>”You know, folk around here have got you figured for a ruthless bitch after that stunt with Diamo. But I know better. Someone hurts those you love, you’ll not forgive it. But underneath it all, you’re a good sort, Corvere.”<br />Mia kissed Ash’s cheek, smiling. “Don’t tell anyone. I’ve a reputation to uphold.”</i><br /><br /><i>”And then she leaned in slow, cupped Mia’s face, and kissed her gently on the lips. It lasted a moment too long. Perhaps not long enough? Warm and soft and honeysweet. Before Mia could decide, it was already over.”</i><br /> <br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br />Where do I even begin?! This was something totally unique and if you ask me I can’t compare it to anything I ever read. The premise of the story might have sounded a lot like all the other assassin books I ever heard of, but Jay Kristoff managed to give it an incomparable spin and I’m very glad I picked this up. It was dark and at times brutal, it was gory and X-rated, there was a lot of cussing and smoking involved and... I loved it! *lol* Enough said! If you enjoy books like that I’m sure you’ll devour this too! ;-)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9408350548214213769" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2773385875" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2773385875" />
    <a title="Sean Barrs " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs"><img alt="Sean Barrs " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605281953p2/27788046.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2773385875?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean Barrs " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean Barrs " href="/user/show/27788046-sean-barrs">Sean Barrs </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780008179991" href="/book/show/29845906-nevernight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=5-star-reads">5-star-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27788046-sean-barrs?shelf=reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review">reviewed-for-fantasy-book-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2773385875" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7194293450559102097"><b>If the <i>Harry Potter Series</i> and <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora</i> ever got together and decided to have a dark book baby, they would call it <i>Nevernight.</i></b><br/><br/> This is the sort of book I dream about reading. Only a fantasy expert could have written one this well. It’s exactly why authors such as Brandon Sanderson and Patrick Rothfuss are so successful: they know their audience. And here Jay Kristoff certainly knew his. <br/><br/>Nevernight captured my heart in all its pure evilness. It’s a wickedly delightful story centre</span>
  <span id="freeText7194293450559102097" style="display:none"><b>If the <i>Harry Potter Series</i> and <i>The Lies of Locke Lamora</i> ever got together and decided to have a dark book baby, they would call it <i>Nevernight.</i></b><br /><br /> This is the sort of book I dream about reading. Only a fantasy expert could have written one this well. It’s exactly why authors such as Brandon Sanderson and Patrick Rothfuss are so successful: they know their audience. And here Jay Kristoff certainly knew his. <br /><br />Nevernight captured my heart in all its pure evilness. It’s a wickedly delightful story centred on a young assassin, Mia, as she learns how to kill with stealth, precision and absolutely no mercy. It’s totally epic through and through. There wasn’t a single low point, just constant highs as I found myself lost in the story and completely invested in all its characters. It’s loaded with betrayals, stabbings and intricate schemes. After finishing it, I read it again before even thinking about moving on to the sequel. Simply because, I wasn’t over it yet. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“The books we love, they love us back. And just as we mark our places in the pages, those pages leave their marks on us. I can see it in you, sure as I see it in me. You're a daughter of the words. A girl with a story to tell.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Mia is attempting to become a blade of the Red Church, an infamous guild of killers. All in order to pursuit her own end goal: murdering those in turn that murdered her family. She is utterly fearless because she possesses a mysteriously dark magic that allows her to control shadows, and in such shadows lurk creatures that have distinct personalities of their own. She has a shadow cat as a familiar who drains all the fear from her giving her a distinct advantage in battle and in training. She is never separate from it and never afraid. <br /><br />Mia takes her own path. Although she is training in an academy with strict rules over life and death, she still finds ways to be herself and not fall into the trap of a brainwashed slave. This made me really like her character. In a way, she is like a darker version of Arya Stark (only more worldly wise and talented.) There’s a fierce competition between her and the other acolytes who are all attempting to become blades. They face off with swords and daggers, with poisons and secrets, in order to become the best of the crop. Only four out of an initial thirty or so will prove themselves worthy and join the elite ranks of the Red Church, never any more year to year. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You'll be a rumor. A whisper. The thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. The last thing you will ever be, girl, is someone's hero.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><br />So, this really does have a lot going for it, though for me what really makes the book stand out is the mystery. Jay Kristoff is a careful writer and he has certainly taken pains not to reveal too much early on. The dark magic that curses through Mia’s blood remains a complete mystery to all. There’s also a lot of hidden surprises here and I don’t doubt there will be more through the rest of the series. In a world of assassins, honestly will only get you so far. And although Mia was played quite significantly here, I think moving forward she has learnt a great deal about people: she has become better at the game of killers. In the next book, I think she will be a much harder person: she has to be. <br /><br />A much deserved 10/10* from me. This is the best fantasy novel I have read in years, I shall be moving straight onto <i>Godsgrave</i> next. <br /><br />_________________________________<br /><br />You can connect with me on social media via <a href="https://linktr.ee/sean.ultra_vegan1" rel="nofollow noopener">My Linktree</a>.<br />__________________________________</span>
  <a data-text-id="7194293450559102097" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1817949745" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer17806916729570666494">Mia is an assassin (in training) who can do alllll kinds of cool shit with her shadow.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527433803ra/25605199.gif' width='350' height='320' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>And she has a talking cat.</b><br/>How do you get better than <i>that</i>?<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527433592ra/25605189.gif' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>How about using an actual <i>blood bath</i> to travel around!?<br/>Yeah. Sure, it's not exactly as quick or clean as pressing a button on your suit and saying, <b>Beam me up, Scotty!</b>, but we are talking about assassins in a world of magic, after all.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527952752ra/25639129.gif' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok. I was expecting this to be all dark and stabby - and it was! But what I wasn't expecting was all the <i>tongue in cheek</i> </span>
  <span id="freeText17806916729570666494" style="display:none">Mia is an assassin (in training) who can do alllll kinds of cool shit with her shadow.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527433803ra/25605199.gif" width="350" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>And she has a talking cat.</b><br>How do you get better than <i>that</i>?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527433592ra/25605189.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>How about using an actual <i>blood bath</i> to travel around!?<br>Yeah. Sure, it's not exactly as quick or clean as pressing a button on your suit and saying, <b>Beam me up, Scotty!</b>, but we are talking about assassins in a world of magic, after all.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1527952752ra/25639129.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok. I was expecting this to be all dark and stabby - and it was! But what I wasn't expecting was all the <i>tongue in cheek</i> humor. From what I've read in some of the other reviews, I think that threw some people off. And not in a good way. <br>But I really loved it and thought it gave the story a different sort of spin to have all the darkness sitting there beside the silliness. To me, that was a huge bonus in the book's favor, but it may not be your jam, so take that into consideration when you decide whether or not to grab this one.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528470761ra/25688652.gif" width="350" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is told with odd flashbacks (that I loved) and weirdly frivolous footnotes (that I also loved) while Mia slashes and stabs her way through the present day part of the story. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528475855ra/25689265.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm a fan of heroes &amp; heroines who are willing to kill, maybe even <i>enjoy</i> killing, but still have enough humanity left that they only kill the ones they think deserve it.<br>And Mia fits that description.<br><b>To. A. Tee.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1528475931ra/25689275.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>But.</b> Obviously, this isn't going to appeal to everyone.<br>And I can't make up your mind for you. Sorry.<br>I thought it was fantastic...for whatever that's worth.</span>

<div id="review_1999939729" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1999939729" />
    <a title="Robin Hobb" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17730703-robin-hobb"><img alt="Robin Hobb" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442450400p2/17730703.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1999939729?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin Hobb" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin Hobb" href="/user/show/17730703-robin-hobb">Robin Hobb</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">friends who like grim dark, fantasy readers</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1999939729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2410247343459670418">First, my caveat! I think it's important to let other readers know if I received a book for free, or was sent it for comment, or if it was written by a friend. I hope that I don't let such things affect how I read a book, but in these days of commercial hype, I think it's best to be completely transparent!<br/><br/>So, I was sent this book by the editor. <br/><br/>I took several weeks to read this book, not because it didn't grab me, but because it somehow was lost in the guest bedroom when I was in midread. Books </span>
  <span id="freeText2410247343459670418" style="display:none">First, my caveat! I think it's important to let other readers know if I received a book for free, or was sent it for comment, or if it was written by a friend. I hope that I don't let such things affect how I read a book, but in these days of commercial hype, I think it's best to be completely transparent!<br /><br />So, I was sent this book by the editor. <br /><br />I took several weeks to read this book, not because it didn't grab me, but because it somehow was lost in the guest bedroom when I was in midread. Books do have a habit of wandering about my house. <br /><br />This is the tale of a youngster who suffers a devastating and terrifying loss of her family. And born of that loss, gains a dark companion to her days.<br /><br />(Wow. So hard to write this well without a bunch of spoilers!)<br /><br />She decides to seek the skills she will need both for vengeance and in the hopes she can rescue some of those she has lost. To gain those skills, she must first serve a hard apprenticeship, and then attempt to get herself to an almost mythical place and school to continue her training.<br /><br />Okay. That's as close as I'm going to get to spoilers. Asked about this book at a signing, I blurted out that it's like Hogwarts, but with a violence and sex. Not the best blurb I've ever given, yet I do think that it gives a hint to what you will encounter. And I liked, very much, that there is honesty and directness in examining what certain kinds of training would do to a person's mind and morality. Our lead character faces some terribly difficult choices, and she makes them in a way that is believable and wrenching.<br /><br />Office Kat also read this book, and her observation was, "The author really knows his characters. Not once does Mia respond to something in a way that was not completely in tune with who she is."<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2410247343459670418" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2368546232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2368546232" />
    <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz"><img alt="Helena of Eretz ✰" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596076376p2/27036454.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2368546232?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Helena of Eretz ✰" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Helena of Eretz ✰" href="/user/show/27036454-helena-of-eretz">Helena of Eretz ✰</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=greco-roman">greco-roman</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27036454-helena-of-eretz?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2368546232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1567666157283333551"><i>Buddy re-read, part one, with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588789715' rel='nofollow noopener'>Mary</a>!</i> (finally lol :P)<br/><br/><b>“The books we love, they love us back. And just as we mark our places in the pages, those pages leave their marks on us. I can see it in you, sure as I see it in me. You're a daughter of the words. A girl with a story to tell.”</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551333129i/27128507._SY540_.jpg' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>WOW.</i> I don’t think that I have any coherent thoughts at the moment.   What an <b>addicting</b> novel! <br/><br/>This was just a rollercoaster ride from start to finish. I started off enjoying the <b>exquisite writing style</b> and then, the stor</span>
  <span id="freeText1567666157283333551" style="display:none"><i>Buddy re-read, part one, with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2588789715" rel="nofollow noopener">Mary</a>!</i> (finally lol :P)<br><br><b>“The books we love, they love us back. And just as we mark our places in the pages, those pages leave their marks on us. I can see it in you, sure as I see it in me. You're a daughter of the words. A girl with a story to tell.”</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551333129i/27128507._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>WOW.</i> I don’t think that I have any coherent thoughts at the moment.   What an <b>addicting</b> novel! <br><br>This was just a rollercoaster ride from start to finish. I started off enjoying the <b>exquisite writing style</b> and then, the story crescendoed into something more, keeping me perched at the edge of my seat in anticipation of what’s to come.  <br><br>I’d also like to say that I’m an <i>emotional wreck</i> because everyone that I thought I trusted...turned out to be someone else entirely, complete with unsavoury agendas. I’m also very sad because I lost a few beloved characters and a number of my ships crashed and burned. <i>WHY???!</i> <b>*cries*</b> Thank you, oh so very much, Jay Kristoff! Grrr….<br><br>So, what’s this <b>brilliant book</b> about?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551333129i/27128508._SY540_.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Mia Corvere</b> originated from a respectable family…that is, until her father is <i>hanged</i> for his part in a rebellion. At age ten, the life that she had always known and the family that she held dear were ripped away from her in a moment. It is then that she avows to seek <b>revenge</b> upon all those who had wronged her and her family. <br><br><i>“Never flinch…Never fear. And never, ever forget.”</i>'<br><br>In order to <b>avenge</b> her family, however, Mia must acquire training in the brutal art of <b>assassination</b>. As a result, she seeks tutelage at the <i>Red Church</i>, where she learns all that she can, so that she can begin checking off the names on her list. But first, now that she has chosen Red Church, the Red Church must choose her. If she wants to become a true assassin, she must be at the top of one of the four classes: <b>blades, poisons, manipulation, or thievery</b>. Does Mia have what it takes to exact her revenge?<br><br><i>“Beauty you're born with, but brains you earn.”</i> <br><br>I’d like to give a shout-out to <b>Mr Kindly</b>, the talking cat, made of shadows! &lt;3 He’s Mia’s <i>secret weapon</i>, who feeds upon her fear and provides some much-needed sassy commentary! ;) Mia also appears to have some <b>magical abilities</b>, where she can <i>control the shadows</i> themselves…<i>SO COOL!</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1539260810ra/26433793.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Furthermore, I really loved the <b>sweet romance</b> between <b>Tric</b> and <b>Mia</b>…And by the way, <i>I DEMAND AN ANSWER ABOUT THAT ENDING!!!</i> Anddddd...<i>bonus points</i> for <b>sexy times!</b> ;)<br><br>I definitely appreciated the balance of <i>light and dark scenes</i> throughout the novel, which prevented it from being either too happy or too sad. I will admit though, that it took me until <b>Chapter 8</b>, before I fell head-over-heels for this book, because it took a while to get accustomed to the <b>purple prose-esque writing style</b> (very much in the vein of Laini Taylor, in my opinion…but x 100!) and the <b>abundance of footnotes</b>. I found the footnotes to be rather <i>unnecessary</i>, albeit interesting. I initially read this book in an e-book format, which meant that all of the footnotes were collected at the end of the chapter. By the time that I got there, I had no idea as to what Jay Kristoff was referring to anymore! Ugh. After a while, I just stopped trying to read them, and it didn’t hinder my understanding of the world, plot, or characters at all. <br><br>On the other hand, I did really enjoy the <b>mythology</b> that was included in this world and the fact that it was a world of <b>three rotating suns</b> (hence the title, <i>Nevernight</i>), as well. And my Ancient Roman-loving heart was in complete adoration of Kristoff's <b>Ancient Roman-esque society</b>, complete with a Senate and legionnaires. <i>I'M ALL HERE FOR IT!</i> I swear that I'll die of happiness if gladiators and chariot races come into play in the future! &lt;3<br><br>Also, in addition to the quote at the start of this review, there is another that especially resonates with me: <b>“Too many books. Too few centuries.”</b> Isn’t that the truth?! ;)<br><br>All things considered, this was an <b>extraordinary book</b> that I highly recommend it to anyone who is literate...seriously. xD I even completely ignored studying for a <i>very important</i> midterm in order to finish this <b>riveting tale</b>. If that doesn’t persuade you, I don’t know what will! :P <br><br>I <i>can't wait</i> to start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32055872.Godsgrave__The_Nevernight_Chronicle___2_" title="Godsgrave (The Nevernight Chronicle, #2) by Jay Kristoff" rel="nofollow noopener">Godsgrave</a>! &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="1567666157283333551" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2007824855" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2007824855" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2007824855?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Elle by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/42130592-chai">chai ♡</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gay-genre-fiction">gay-genre-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-high-fantasy">sff-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=genre-experiments">genre-experiments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sapphic-books-shelf">sapphic-books-shelf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2007824855" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9385956700856572286"><b>my loyal followers:</b> Elle, why are you giving 4 1/2 stars to a book that took you almost four months to read<br/><b>me, grabbing this book and hiding it in my jacket:</b> I do what I want<br/><br/>Honestly... okay. I’d pitch this book as Hogwarts for assassins and I enjoyed it so much. <br/><br/>♔ <b>This is a book about becoming yourself,</b> on more levels than one. It’s about developing an ethical code when you’ve had it trained out of you, and synthesizing your childhood self and your self after immense trauma. I love the explorat</span>
  <span id="freeText9385956700856572286" style="display:none"><b>my loyal followers:</b> Elle, why are you giving 4 1/2 stars to a book that took you almost four months to read<br /><b>me, grabbing this book and hiding it in my jacket:</b> I do what I want<br /><br />Honestly... okay. I’d pitch this book as Hogwarts for assassins and I enjoyed it so much. <br /><br />♔ <b>This is a book about becoming yourself,</b> on more levels than one. It’s about developing an ethical code when you’ve had it trained out of you, and synthesizing your childhood self and your self after immense trauma. I love the exploration of Mia‘s faith crisis. Throughout the book, we are told that she used to be a believer and is no longer sure if she is.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“This makes you who you are. She punched the slab of muscle above his heart. “This." She slapped the top of his head. "These.” The girl took hold of his hands not in front of him, staring into the boys eyes. “Slavemarks. Tattoos. Scars. What you look like doesn’t change who you are inside. They can give you a new face, but they can’t give you a new heart. No matter what they take from you, they can’t take that away unless you let them. That’s real strength, Tric. That’s real power.”</i>
</blockquote><br />And god, Mia has so much potential for book two. Guys, I am so excited. <b>She’s developed so much just in this book and I can’t wait for more of her arc.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Iron or glass? they'd ask.<br />She was neither.<br />She was steel.”</i>
</blockquote><br />♚ If we’re talking about romance… <b>spoilers.</b> Please skip this paragraph. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tric is a decent romantic interest, but my spoiler-addled lesbian mind is <i>really</i> happy about the love interest change. I do think spoilers about later developments ruined Tric a bit for me. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />♔ <i>Nevernight</i> is so, so hilarious. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1719090866" rel="nofollow noopener">Why are murder books always so funny.</a><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Cock is just another word for ‘fool.’ But you call someone a cunt, well…” The girl smiled. “You’re implying a sense of malice there. An intent. Malevolent and self-aware. Don’t think I name Consul Scaeva a cunt to gift him insult. Cunts have brains, Don Tric. Cunts have teeth. Someone calls you a cunt, you take it as a compliment. As a sign that folk believe you’re not to be lightly fucked with.” A shrug. “I think they call that irony.”</i>
</blockquote><br />♔ The worldbuilding here was <i>super interesting</i> after around page 100, but up till then I found it <b>confusing and convoluted.</b> I understand that thrown-in worldbuilding is a style. I enjoy thrown-in worldbuilding. Christ, guys, <i>Six of Crows</i> is my favorite book of all time and I STILL have yet to read the Grisha. But with <i>Six of Crows,</i> I felt the tension and character work even when I didn’t know what was happening. I got invested in the world from the beginning. It can be done. <b>Jay Kristoff didn't do it for me.</b><br /><br />♚ Related to the last point - <b>the first 100 pages are overwritten bullshit.</b> I know you guys are going to come at me for this and I completely do not care; <b>it needed editing.</b> While I found parts interesting, especially the footnotes - I know people complain about those but they were the only thing I liked - on the whole, the initial section was too long, had little to no tension, was totally overwritten even compared to the rest of the book, and offered barely any character development compared to worldbuilding. <br /><br />♔ After all that, I just <i>loved</i> it. <i>Nevernight</i> is <i>so</i> engaging and so non-boring after its beginning section. <b>I could barely put it down.</b><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Beauty you're born with, but brains you earn.”</i>
</blockquote><br />♔ The plot twists are just as awesome as everyone says, but I have to admit, <b>I think you can like this novel even if you get spoiled.</b> Proof? <b>I got spoiled about one of the twists and still a) loved the book and b) think it’s a brilliant twist.</b><br /><br />Listen, guys, after the admittedly crappy first 100 pages, I just could not put this down. This is one of those times you just gotta defer to the wisdom of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42130592-kazzy-boy" rel="nofollow noopener">your fellow trusted gays who spoiled you for all the big plot twists</a> and enjoy yourself. The plotline was amazing, the characters compelling, and the themes teased made me so happy. <b>I cannot wait for book two.</b> (And update, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2097185918?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">of course I loved it</a>.)<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/girladamparrish" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9385956700856572286" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=epic-fantasy">epic-fantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=reread">reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297359924" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2118216435250694517"><b>REREAD: October, 2017</b><br/><br/>This news just in: <b>this book is fucking fantastic.</b><br/><br/>I wanted to reread this in preparation for Godsgrave because I remember <i>nothing</i>, mate. Please, I barely remember a book 2 days after finishing ok. <b>I also decided to try the audio</b> and besssst decision of LIFE. The audiobook is absolutely brilliant! Accents and emotions and <i>everything</i>. 10/10 for this audio. ACTUALLY 10/10 FOR THE WHOLE GODDAMN BOOK. THIS IS SO FREAKING BLOODY. It gets the full five stars and all my previous mur</span>
  <span id="freeText2118216435250694517" style="display:none"><b>REREAD: October, 2017</b><br /><br />This news just in: <b>this book is fucking fantastic.</b><br /><br />I wanted to reread this in preparation for Godsgrave because I remember <i>nothing</i>, mate. Please, I barely remember a book 2 days after finishing ok. <b>I also decided to try the audio</b> and besssst decision of LIFE. The audiobook is absolutely brilliant! Accents and emotions and <i>everything</i>. 10/10 for this audio. ACTUALLY 10/10 FOR THE WHOLE GODDAMN BOOK. THIS IS SO FREAKING BLOODY. It gets the full five stars and all my previous murmurs of disapprovals are gone. <br /><br />I am just here for it, ok. It is so so bloody and <i>clever</i> and Mia has got to be one of the best female anti-heroes of all. And Mister Kindly is everything. And whoever the narrator is with his footnotes is so absolutely <i>salty</i> the whole time. I LOVE IT.<br /><br /><b>Anyway. I was adorable last year with my cute mixed feelings. Now I just love it.</b> Now I shall go arm myself with a butter knife (I fierce ok) and wait at my mailbox for Godsgrave to arrive.<br /><br />(Also can I just say that more fantasy needs to be written by sassy sarcastic narrators? Because need.)<br /><br /><br />****<br /><br /><b>1st READ REVIEW: November, 2016</b><br /><br />Oh this shall be a very very hard review to write. Why? <b>I AM ALL A MIX OF GOOD AND BAD FEELINGS.</b> I was waiting for it to explode my mind and it just...didn't?? But at the same time it was endlessly addicting and I found myself arguing with the clock on whether I should sleep or read. (Loooool to the clock. OF COURSE I READ.) But I can't ignore my quibbles. So. Excuse me while I have a life crisis.<br /><br /><b>So basically it's an ASSASSIN ORIGIN STORY.</b> Which is, actually, my favourite. Which means (A) it's brutal, (B) it's bloody, and (C) it's stabby. All excellent things. Lovely. But I came a bit <i>stuck</i> here anyway...for the simple reason I just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17910124.The_Emperor_s_Blades__Chronicle_of_the_Unhewn_Throne___1_" title="The Emperor's Blades (Chronicle of the Unhewn Throne, #1) by Brian Staveley" rel="nofollow noopener">The Emperor's Blades</a> WHICH WAS SO FREAKING FANTASTIC I NEARLY DIED OF FEELS and I couldn't help comparing them. The Emperor's Blades also had an assassin/training storyline and it was just WAY MORE TOUGH AND BRUTAL than anything Nevernight was dishing up. Hence I felt Nevernight was a bit weak there in the assassin training stuff. Yeeeeeah. I know. I'm the worst.<br /><br />So YES it was bloody and stabby. But it felt like it was holding back...which doesn't makes sense <b>because it's adult and not YA.</b><br /><br />(Also a note on the "adult fantasy" bit...<b>YES IT IS ADULT NOT YA.</b> Just for the detailed sex scenes I think, and the violence.)<br /><br /><b>I did really really love Mia though!!</b> She had the potential to be one of those "emotionless assassins who stands on their own and knows no soul" but gahhh NO MIA WAS TOTALLY AWESOME. She was a complete tangle of sheer brutality and stabtastic stabbiness (shh that's so a term) but at the same time she actually <i>cared about things</i>. She SHOWED SHE CARED. And she managed to do so while also threatening to stab people so. #win <b>And she also can manipulate shadows.</b> She's called a "darkin" and do we get to know the extent or reason for her powers? HAHAHHAHAHAH NO LITTLE LAMB. We get to frown and ask questions. Where is mine sequel. Bring it thusly here.<br /><br /><b>I also <i>loved</i> the footnotes.</b> Okay they were tedious at times. Sometimes I was torn between "is this world building freaking fantastic with so much detail??" and "is this as tedious as eating a banana smoothie with a whisk??" AND HONESTLY I'M STILL TORN. But half the time the footnotes were had <b>this sarcastic commentary going on</b> and sarcasm is what I live for. (I mean, I also live for cake. But. Let's not get off track here.)<br /><br /><b>And the romance?!</b> Okay it was definitely a good romance, because it was slow burn and started off as friendship AND I PRETTY MUCH PANICKED OVER IT THE FULL TIME. Two assassins competing for a few positions in the top of the assassin school?? But also falling in love??? I MEAN, I LOVE PANICKING. THAT'S COOL. <b>I loved Tric!</b> He was adorable and kind of squishy and <i>so so sweet</i> and managed to be freaking badass and frightening at the same time. All the love for Tric.<br /><br /><b>AND THERE IS A TALKING CAT.</b> Well, a talking not-cat because it's made out of shadows, but it is literally my favourite thing. All the stars for just the cat.<br /><br /><b>OKAY BUT NOW WE GOTTA TALK ABOUT THE PROBLEMS...</b> And I shall have a handy dandy list because I'm kind like that. (Yes yes you're welcome.)<br /><br />• <b>It was very predictable.</b> Have I read too many books? Or just too many assassin stories?? WHO KNOWS. But I called a ton of the plot twists ahead of time. (Not the BIGGEST one at the end though.) And I saw all the foreshadowing and just...eh. I was never socked in the face with shock.<br />• <b>Also the deaths were totally predictable.</b> This means my feels WERE NOT CRUMPLED because I was prepared the whole time???? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I <i>knew</i> Tric was going to die. I just knew it. I'M STILL SAD BECAUSE I LOVED HIM SO MUCH. But I was preparing for his death the moment I saw him??? So yeah. And I figured most of the cooler acolytes were going to die. And I didn't really think about Cassius, but I didn't KNOW HIM so I didn't care that he died. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• <b>Mia makes a COMPLETELY BIZARRE DECISION at the end that I still don't understand.</b> It was so out of character for her, I'm lowkey angry??? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She went all that way, killed all those people, fought, nearly died, had her family's honour to avenge which had driven her for 6 years....and then she gets to the end and can't kill a random boy? LIKE SHE'D KILLED TONS OF PEOPLE WHEN SHE WAS A YOUNG GIRL. WHAT IS THIS. It didn't make sense. She wasn't a golden hearted angel. Why did she baulk? I suppose it was to show us she was "truly human inside" or blah blah something like that. But I thought it was downright incomprehensible. It also has come to my attention that I'm a psychopath probably. Excuse me while I go scream into a pillow. (PS. It really didn't make sense why she chose not to kill that random dude, okay??? She killed so many people later too??? What's going on???) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />• <b>The plot literally DIED in favour of sexy times.</b> Like, sure, haha, we didn't neeeeed to have a plot line continuing around when we could just have super detailedly graphic sex scenes. OF COURSE NOT. (Also is currently breaking plates in the background.) Look I'm not fond of reading sex scenes anyway, but that wasn't the problem for me: the problem was there was literally no plot happening about 2/3rds through the book because all we had was Mia thinking about seeeeeex all the time. I WAS BORED AND DISAPPOINTED.<br />• <b>It made everyone "beautiful".</b> I just hate this trope. I still see it a lot and I think it's dangerous and poisonous. Like who defines beautiful??? GIVE ME A BREAK. Mia had to get a magical facelift and a boob job and I just...I'm so annoyed.<br /><br /><br /><br /><b>But like I said: I COULDN'T ACTUALLY PUT IT DOWN.</b> The writing was really good and captivating, even if the plot was sometimes running off to nap in a daisy field of nothingness. Mia was epic. Tric was epic. <b>There was so much SASS.</b> And so much stab. AND OMG DID I MENTION THERE ARE <i>THREE</i> BEAUTIFUL MAPS??????? That just wins my heart and soul to be honest.<br /><br /><b>I'M VERY GLAD I READ IT.</b> I am definitely keen for the sequel too! I have a lot of quibbles and there were several times when I felt very MAD at the book. But excellent writing and characters and EXCELLENT SASS and excellent amounts of the #stabstabstab outweighs the negatives for me so I shall be over here, wishing I had a talking cat, and also petting the beauty that is the hardcover copy omg.<br /><br /><br />*** QUOTES ***<br /><br /><blockquote>"If I were going to name my blade," Mia said thoughtfully, "I'd call it 'Fluffy'."<br />Tric snorted with laughter. "Fluffy?"<br />"'Byss, yes," the girl nodded. "Think of the terror you'd instil. Being bested by a foe wielding a sword called Souldrinker...<i>that</i> you could live with. Imagine the shame of having the piss smacked out of you by a blade called Fluffy." </blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"I've got tea," Mercurio sighed. "And cake."<br />The girl covered her growling belly with both palms.<br />"...What kind of cake?"<br />"The free kind."<br />Mia pouted. Licked her lips and tasted blood.<br />"My favourite."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Mia stepped inside, and for the third time that turn, felt her lungs bid her breath farewell. She stood on a mezzanine overlooking a dark wood -- a forest of ornate shelves, laid out like a garden maze. And on each shelf stood books. Piles of books. Mountains of books. Oceans and oceans of books. Books of stained vellum and fresh parchment. Books bound in leather and wood and leaves, locked books and dusty books, books as thick as her waist and as tiny as her fist. Mia's eyes were alight, fingernails denting the wooden railing.<br />"Naev, don't let me down there," she breathed.<br />"Why not?"<br />"You'll never see me again..."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"There's not enough places among the Blades for all of us, Mia. Technically we're in competition with each other. Why would I help you?"<br />"Because I said please?"<br />"...You didn't say please."<br />Mia waved her hand. "A mere technicality."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Practising?" she sneered. "You'd be better off praying."<br />"Apologies," Mia frowned, searching the floor as if looking for something. "I appear to have misplaced the fucks I give for what you think..."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>Mia dragged deep on her cigarillo. "You don't think this is the kind of thing the Ministry should mention on your first turn? 'O, by the by, Acolytes, there's these colossal fucking wormthings that live in the library, so for Maw's sake, get your books back on time'?"</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="2118216435250694517" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2484576801" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2484576801" />
    <a title="Hamad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad"><img alt="Hamad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577880699p2/54464244.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2484576801?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hamad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hamad" href="/user/show/54464244-hamad">Hamad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780008179984" href="/book/show/34503674-nevernight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=gifts">gifts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=paperbacks">paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=e-books">e-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=good-covers">good-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54464244-hamad?shelf=recommendations">recommendations</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2484576801" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5344283519733989946"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href='https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/07/06/nevernight-review/' rel='nofollow noopener'>@The Book Prescription</a><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“The brighter the light, the deeper the shadow.” </i>
</b><br/><br/>🌟 Lo and behold, it looks like I am still capable of giving books 5 stars, even if it takes me 6 months and 60 books to do so! Nevernight is currently my favorite book for this year and also is joining my favorite books of all times list!<br/><br/>🌟 I have added this book to my TBR since it first came out and it has been there for 3 years now. I have seen very mixed reviews a</span>
  <span id="freeText5344283519733989946" style="display:none"> This review and other non-spoilery reviews can be found <a href="https://thebookprescription.wordpress.com/2019/07/06/nevernight-review/" rel="nofollow noopener">@The Book Prescription</a><br /><br /><b>
  <i>“The brighter the light, the deeper the shadow.” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 Lo and behold, it looks like I am still capable of giving books 5 stars, even if it takes me 6 months and 60 books to do so! Nevernight is currently my favorite book for this year and also is joining my favorite books of all times list!<br /><br />🌟 I have added this book to my TBR since it first came out and it has been there for 3 years now. I have seen very mixed reviews about the book and one reviewer I trust gave it 1 star and another reviewer I trust gave it 5 stars! It was so confusing and then Sara picked this up for me for my 10 bloggers, 10 recommendations I did this year and I loved this.<br /><br />🌟 As soon as I started reading this, a clear picture was forming for why is this such a controversial book, I admit that the author has a purple prose that you either love or hate! The opening line is powerful and shows that the story has such a great potential. I was provoked by some of the flowery sentences and wanted to throw the books but patience is key here and some of my friends told me it gets better and I am glad they did. I did not consider DNFing the book because as I will explain here, it had excellent characters and plot and everything, only the writing was a bit off at first!<br /><br />🌟 After the first part (After page ~130) the writing is much much better and there are plenty of great quotes. The book was funny but not to the point that it became silly! There is also the footnotes that may be annoying at first, but they are easy to get used to and the further you read, the less of these you will have!<br /><br /> <b>
  <i> “You’ll be a rumor. A whisper. The thought that wakes the bastards of this world sweating in the nevernight. The last thing you will ever be, girl, is someone’s hero.” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 I love a book with good characters, and this book had some of the most memorable characters I ever read! I love Mia the MC, a female teen protagonist that was not annoying as uusal. The other characters were all great too, many of them die but we’re keeping this spoiler free.<br /><br />🌟 The world building was effing amazing!!! I really appreciate it when authors take the time to think about all the little details. In Nevernight world there are 3 suns and there is almost no night and the terminology and the mythology that the author built upon those facts is crazy! I just get mind blown when I think about the effort it takes to get everything right.<br /><br /> <b>
  <i> “The Light is full of lies, Acolyte. The Suns serve only to blind us.” </i>
</b><br /><br />🌟 And finally, as someone who loves good plot twists, this had many awesome ones! The plot twists did not come out of nowhere and the build up for plot twists on the last pages started on page 1. My legs were shaking while reading this and this is a sign of me being anxious! I was so absorbed into the story and I did care about everyone.<br /><br />🌟 Summary: Nevernight is as good as a story can be, patience is needed to get used to things for the first 100 pages, the prose and footnotes may be distracting but I promise it is worth it. This book hit all the right notes and I am going to read Godsgrave very very soon!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5344283519733989946" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
